{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /config/.claude/skills/sc-task-unified-protocol\n\n> **NOTE**: Classification has already been performed by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The classification header has already been emitted. Do NOT emit it again. This skill handles **execution only** for STANDARD and STRICT tier tasks.\n>\n> If for any reason no classification header was emitted before this skill was invoked, emit one now using ONLY the tier values STRICT, STANDARD, LIGHT, or EXEMPT (no other values are valid).\n\n# /sc:task-unified - Unified Task Execution with Compliance\n\n## Purpose\n\nUnified command that merges orchestration capabilities with MCP compliance enforcement. Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [████████░░] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"⚠️ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 4.5 Test Failure Escalation Protocol (TFEP)\n\n**CRITICAL**: When tests fail during the Verification Phase (Section 4), agents MUST follow this protocol. Ad-hoc fixes are PROHIBITED.\n\n#### TFEP Prohibition Rules (VIOLATION-level)\n\nThese rules apply to ALL compliance tiers that run tests (STRICT, STANDARD):\n\n1. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT fix any code in response to test failures without completing the TFEP workflow.\n2. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT modify test expectations to make failing tests pass without adversarial validation.\n3. **VIOLATION**: Ad-hoc patches derived from test output are PROHIBITED. The agent must not read a traceback and immediately edit code to resolve it.\n\n**Permitted Exceptions** (MAY fix directly without TFEP):\n- Single `ImportError`/`NameError` in test scaffolding the agent just wrote, affecting <=2 tests, where the error is in the test file itself (not in implementation code).\n- Lint/formatting failures (trivially fixable, unambiguous root cause).\n- Deprecation warnings (not failures).\n\n**Valid Adversarial Outcome**: \"Test expectations are wrong\" is a legitimate conclusion from adversarial debate. When the debate concludes that test expectations are outdated rather than the code being wrong, this is NOT grounds for the agent to directly edit the tests — it must be presented to the user for review.\n\n#### Test Baseline Snapshot (Pre-Implementation)\n\nBefore implementation begins, the agent MUST record a test baseline:\n\n1. Capture the list of all existing test files and test function names at task start (e.g., via `uv run pytest --collect-only -q` or directory listing).\n2. Store this baseline in memory for the duration of the task.\n3. On any test failure, classify each failing test as:\n   - **Pre-existing**: Test name appears in the baseline (existed before this task).\n   - **New**: Test name does NOT appear in the baseline (written by the agent during this task).\n4. This classification drives the MUST-escalate vs MAY-fix-directly decision below.\n\n#### Escalation Trigger Detection\n\n**MUST escalate (trigger TFEP):**\n- Any **pre-existing test** fails (tests in the baseline that were not modified by the agent). This is the primary trigger — regressions in existing tests indicate the implementation broke something.\n- **3 or more new tests** fail simultaneously (indicates a systemic issue, not a simple typo).\n- **Runtime exceptions in implementation code** (TypeError, AttributeError, KeyError, etc. in the code being tested, not in the test scaffolding itself).\n\n**Escalation gradient (within-TFEP, for future forensic integration):**\n- Repeated failure (same test cluster fails after fix attempt) → escalate from light to standard\n- Multi-file blast radius from recent changes → escalate\n- Low-confidence root cause from adversarial debate → escalate\n- Unresolved adversarial outcome (no winner/tie) → escalate\n- Second failed retest → escalate\n- Cross-domain or non-obvious regression → escalate\n\n#### TFEP Execution Flow\n\nWhen TFEP triggers, execute the following steps:\n\n**Step 1: Halt and freeze**\n1. **STOP** testing immediately.\n2. **FREEZE** implementation — no further code changes permitted.\n\n**Step 2: Construct failure context**\n3. Build a `failure_context` YAML package containing:\n   - `test_names`: list of failing test function names\n   - `test_files`: list of test files containing failures\n   - `error_output`: full traceback/error output\n   - `expected_behavior`: what was expected\n   - `actual_behavior`: what actually happened\n   - `changes_made`: files changed during this task with descriptions\n   - `task_description`: current task description\n   - `test_baseline`: the pre-implementation test baseline\n   - `escalation_count`: which TFEP trigger this is (1, 2, or 3)\n4. Write context to `{output_dir}/context.yaml`.\n\n**Step 3: Invoke forensic**\n5. Determine the forensic tier based on escalation count:\n   - 1st trigger → `--tier light --intent triage`\n   - 2nd trigger → `--tier standard`\n   - 3rd trigger → **FULL STOP**. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n6. Invoke: `/sc:forensic --tier {tier} --intent triage --caller task-unified --context {context_path} --output {output_dir} --depth quick`\n7. The forensic pipeline runs autonomously through all its phases and returns a structured return contract.\n\n**Step 4: Consume forensic results**\n8. Read the forensic return contract from `{output_dir}/return-contract.yaml`.\n9. Handle based on status:\n   - If `test_is_wrong == true`: Present to user for review. Do NOT auto-fix tests.\n   - If `status == \"success\"`: Proceed to Step 5 (tasklist insertion).\n   - If `status == \"partial\"` or `recommended_escalation != \"none\"`: Increment `escalation_count` and return to Step 3.\n   - If `status == \"failed\"`: Report to user, halt execution.\n\n**Step 5: Tasklist insertion**\n10. Read `tasklist_insertion_path` from the return contract.\n11. Insert the remediation block into the current tasklist:\n    - Add `## Failure Remediation Plan (Adjudicated)` heading.\n    - Insert remediation tasks BEFORE existing test/verification tasks.\n    - Preserve original tasklist structure — append, don't replace.\n\n**Step 6: Resume**\n12. Resume execution with `--compliance strict` starting from the inserted remediation tasks.\n13. After remediation tasks complete, re-run the original test suite.\n14. If tests pass: TFEP resolved successfully. Produce incident report and continue.\n15. If tests fail again: Increment `escalation_count`, return to Step 2.\n\n#### TFEP Incident Reporting\n\nAfter each TFEP resolution (success or escalation), produce `tfep-incident-report.md`:\n\n```markdown\n# TFEP Incident Report\n\n- **Trigger**: {which threshold rule fired}\n- **Escalation count**: {1, 2, or 3}\n- **Failing tests**: {test names and classification}\n- **Root cause**: {summary from rca-verdict.md}\n- **Solution**: {summary from solution-verdict.md}\n- **Outcome**: {success / escalated / failed}\n- **Forensic artifacts**: {path to output_dir}\n```\n\nThis report is committed to git alongside other forensic artifacts.\n\n#### Escalation Budget\n\n```\n1st TFEP trigger  → /sc:forensic --tier light --intent triage    (~5-8K tokens)\n2nd TFEP trigger  → /sc:forensic --tier standard                 (~15-20K tokens)\n3rd TFEP trigger  → FULL STOP. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n```\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist enforced\n-> Verification agent spawned\n-> Adversarial questions answered\n```\n\n### STANDARD Task\n```\n/sc:task \"add pagination to user list\"\n\n-> Classified as STANDARD (add keyword, typical keyword, documentation path)\n-> Quick sanity check only\n-> No verification delay\n```\n\n### EXEMPT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"explain how the auth flow works\"\n\n-> Classified as EXEMPT (explain pattern detected)\n-> Immediate execution\n-> No compliance overhead\n```\n\n### Override Example\n```\n/sc:task \"update config file\" --compliance strict\n\n-> User override to STRICT regardless of classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide confidence scoring with rationale\n- Track feedback for continuous calibration\n- Support user overrides with justification\n\n**Will Not:**\n- Skip safety-critical verification for STRICT tasks\n- Verify during Phase 2; not a blocker.` (OQ-4)\n    63→- **Impact**: The spec's dependency map shows `sprint/config.py` as a modified file, but the roadmap's Files Modified table does not list it. If SprintConfig actually lives in `sprint/models.py`, the spec's dependency map is wrong. If it lives in `sprint/config.py`, the roadmap's file manifest is incomplete. Update the spec's dependency map or the roadmap's file manifest accordingly to eliminate ambiguity.\n    65→\n    66→### DEV-007\n    67→- **ID**: DEV-007\n    68→- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n    69→- **Deviation**: Roadmap defers `--skip-wiring-gate` CLI flag; spec explicitly includes it in Phase 2 rollout\n    70→- **Spec Quote**: `Override available via --skip-wiring-gate flag` (Section 8, Phase 2: Soft)\n    71→- **Roadmap Quote**: `Defer. Problem Statement\n    16→\n    17→The cli-portify executor no-op bug (forensic report, 2026-03-17) demonstrated that\n    18→Link 3 of the fidelity chain (Tasklist -> Code) has zero programmatic coverage. The\n    19→pipeline's gate infrastructure validates documents -- not code integration. Components\n    20→defined in specifications and decomposed into tasks can pass all existing gates while\n    21→producing code where modules are never connected to their consumers.\n    22→\n    23→**The \"defined but not wired\" pattern recurs across multiple systems:**\n    24→\n    25→| System | Evidence |\n    26→|--------|----------|\n    27→| cli-portify executor | `step_runner=None` default; steps exist but are never called |\n    28→| DEVIATION_ANALYSIS_GATE | Defined at `roadmap/gates.py:712` but never wired into `_build_steps()` |\n    29→| SprintGatePolicy | Exists at `sprint/executor.py:46-89` but `build_remediation_step` is not invoked from the sprint loop |\n    30→| Trailing gate framework | `TrailingGateRunner` exists but `execute_sprint()` never calls it |\n    31→\n    32→**This release creates the first code-level gate in the pipeline.**\n    33→\n    34→---\n    35→\n    36→## 2. Goals and Non-Goals\n    37→\n    38→### Goals\n    39→\n    40→1. Detect unwired injectable dependencies (`Optional[Callable] = None` never provided at any call site)\n    41→2. Detect orphan modules (exported functions never imported by any consumer)\n    42→3. Detect unwired dispatch registries (dictionary entries mapping to non-importable functions)\n    43→4. Emit a structured YAML report compatible with the `GateCriteria`/`SemanticCheck` pattern\n    44→5. Deploy in shadow mode initially, with a path to soft and full enforcement\n    45→\n    46→### Non-Goals (v1.0)\n    47→\n    48→- No-op fallback detection (deferred to v1.1 pending shadow-mode data)\n    49→- Cross-language analysis (Python only)\n    50→- Runtime behavioral verification (see Smoke Test Gate proposal)\n    51→- Dynamic dispatch resolution (`**kwargs`, `getattr`, `importlib`)\n    52→- Modifying the `SemanticCheck` interface (no `pre_checks` in this release)\n    53→\n    54→---\n    55→\n    56→## 3. Architecture\n    57→\n    58→### 3.1 System Context\n    59→\n    60→```\n    61→Existing Pipeline Infrastructure          New Component\n    62→================================          =============\n    63→\n    64→pipeline/models.py                        audit/wiring_gate.py\n    65→  GateCriteria ─────────────────────────>   WIRING_GATE (constant)\n    66→  SemanticCheck ────────────────────────>   check functions\n    67→\n    68→pipeline/gates.py\n    69→  gate_passed() ────────────────────────>   evaluates WIRING_GATE\n    70→\n    71→sprint/executor.py\n    72→  SprintGatePolicy ─────────────────────>   invokes wiring checks post-task\n    73→\n    74→pipeline/trailing_gate.py\n    75→  TrailingGateRunner ───────────────────>   deferred evaluation (shadow mode)\n    76→  resolve_gate_mode() ──────────────────>   scope-aware enforcement\n    77→```\n    78→\n    79→### 3.2 Module Architecture\n    80→\n    81→```\n    82→src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py    (NEW -- core analysis)\n    83→    |\n    84→    |--- WiringFinding (dataclass)\n    85→    |--- WiringReport (dataclass)\n    86→    |--- WiringConfig\n   101→```\n   102→\n   103→### 3.3 Data Flow\n   104→\n   105→```\n   106→                    +-----------------+\n   107→                    | Task completes  |\n   108→                          |\n   118→                             v\n   119→                +------------+------------+\n   120→                | run_wiring_analysis()   |\n   121→                |                         |\n   122→                | 1. analyze_unwired_     |\n   123→                |    callables()          |\n   124→                | 2. analyze_orphan_      |\n   125→ wiring-report.md     |\n   134→                | (YAML frontmatter +     |\n   135→                |  finding details)       |\n   136→                +------------+------------+\n   137→ block    |\n   150→                    +--------+--------+\n   151→```\n   152→\n   153→---\n   154→\n   155→## 4. Detailed Design\n   156→\n   157→### 4.1 Data Models\n   158→\n   159→```python\n   160→# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py\n   161→\n   162→from __future__ import annotations\n   163→\n   164→import ast\n   165→import re\n   166→from dataclasses import dataclass, field\n   167→from pathlib import Path\n   168→from typing import Literal\n   169→\n   170→from ..pipeline.models import GateCriteria, SemanticCheck\n   171→\n   172→\n   173→@dataclass\n   174→class WiringFinding:\n   175→    \"\"\"A single wiring verification finding.\"\"\"\n   176→\n   177→    finding_type: Literal[\"unwired_callable\", \"orphan_module\", \"unwired_registry\"]\n   178→    file_path: str\n   179→    symbol_name: str\n   180→    line_number: int\n   181→    detail: str\n   182→    severity: Literal[\"critical\", \"major\"] = \"critical\"\n   183→\n   184→    def to_dict(self) -> dict[str, str | int]:\n   185→        return {\n   186→            \"finding_type\": self.finding_type,\n   187→            \"file_path\": self.file_path,\n   188→            \"symbol_name\": self.symbol_name,\n   189→            \"line_number\": self.line_number,\n   190→            \"detail\": self.detail,\n   191→            \"severity\": self.severity,\n   192→        }\n   193→\n   194→\n   195→@dataclass\n   196→class WiringReport:\n   197→    \"\"\"Aggregate wiring analysis results.\"\"\"\n   198→\n   199→    target_dir: str\n   200→    files_analyzed: int = 0\n   201→    unwired_callables: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   202→    orphan_modules: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   203→    unwired_registries: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   204→\n   205→    @property\n   206→    def unwired_count(self) -> int:\n   207→        return len(self.unwired_callables)\n   208→\n   209→    @property\n   210→    def orphan_count(self) -> int:\n   211→        return len(self.orphan_modules)\n   212→\n   213→    @property\n   214→    def registry_count(self) -> int:\n   215→        return len(self.unwired_registries)\n   216→\n   217→    @property\n   218→    def total_findings(self) -> int:\n   219→        return self.unwired_count + self.orphan_count + self.registry_count\n   220→\n   221→    @property\n   222→    def passed(self) -> bool:\n   223→        return self.total_findings == 0\n   224→```\n   225→\n   226→#### 4.1.1 TurnLedger Extensions\n   227→\n   228→The TurnLedger class (base definition at `sprint/models.py:488-525`) gains wiring-gate-specific\n   229→fields and methods for budget tracking. Generic `debit_gate()`/`credit_gate()` generalization\n   230→is deferred to v3.3.\n   231→\n   232→**New fields** (all with defaults — backward-compatible with existing TurnLedger instances):\n   233→\n   234→```python\n   235→# On TurnLedger (sprint/models.py)\n   236→wiring_gate_cost: int = 0        # Cumulative turns debited for wiring analysis\n   237→wiring_gate_credits: int = 0     # Cumulative turns credited back on pass\n   238→wiring_gate_scope: GateScope = GateScope.TASK  # Scope at which wiring gate operates\n   239→```\n   240→\n   241→**New methods**:\n   242→\n   243→```python\n   244→def debit_wiring(self, turns: int) -> None:\n   245→    \"\"\"Debit turns for wiring analysis execution.\n   246→\n   247→    Called before run_wiring_analysis(). Unconditional — always debits\n   248→    regardless of analysis outcome.\n   249→    \"\"\"\n   250→\n   251→def credit_wiring(self, turns: int, rate: float) -> None:\n   252→    \"\"\"Credit turns back after successful wiring analysis.\n   253→\n   254→    Uses int(turns * reimbursement_rate) which floors to 0 when\n   255→    turns=1 and rate=0.8. Tests must assert wiring_gate_credits == 0\n   256→    for single-turn debits at the default reimbursement rate.\n   257→\n   258→    IMPORTANT: int(turns * reimbursement_rate) floors to 0 when\n   259→    turns=1 and rate=0.8 (since int(0.8) = 0). This means single-turn\n   260→    wiring debits receive zero credit reimbursement. This is by design —\n   261→    the reimbursement_rate is effectively inert for single-turn debits\n   262→    unless set to >= 1.0.\n   263→    \"\"\"\n   264→\n   265→def can_run_wiring_gate(self, cost: int) -> bool:\n   266→    \"\"\"Check if budget allows a wiring gate run of the given cost.\n   267→\n   268→    Returns True if remaining budget >= cost. Used as a pre-check\n   269→    before debit_wiring() to avoid over-budget execution.\n   270→    \"\"\"\n   271→```\n   272→\n   273→### 4.2 Analysis Functions\n   274→\n   275→#### 4.2.1 Unwired Callable Analysis\n   276→\n   277→**Purpose**: Detect constructor parameters typed `Optional[Callable]` (or `Callable | None`)\n   278→with default `None` that are never explicitly provided at any call site in the codebase.\n   279→\n   280→**Algorithm**:\n   281→\n   282→```\n   283→1. AST-parse all Python files in target directory\n   284→2. For each class definition:\n   285→   a. Find __init__ method\n   286→   b. Extract parameters where annotation references Callable with a None default:\n   287→\n   288→      Normalize annotation to string:\n   289→        annotation_str = ast.unparse(param.annotation) if param.annotation else \"\"\n   290→\n   291→      Match using word-boundary pattern (prevents false positives on names\n   292→      containing \"Callable\" as a substring, e.g., NotCallableType):\n   293→        callable_pattern = re.compile(\n   294→            r'\\b(typing\\.)?Callable\\b|'\n   295→            r'\\bcollections\\.abc\\.Callable\\b'\n   296→        )\n   297→\n   298→      Record as injectable if:\n   299→        callable_pattern.search(annotation_str)\n   300→        AND isinstance(param.default, ast.Constant)\n   301→        AND param.default.value is None\n   302→\n   303→      Note: ast.unparse() handles all annotation forms correctly, including\n   304→      ast.Subscript nodes (Optional[Callable[...]]) and manually-quoted\n   305→      forward references (\"Callable[...]\") which render as quoted literals\n   306→      still matchable by the pattern above.\n   307→      Note: from __future__ import annotations does NOT change ast.parse()\n   308→      output — annotations remain AST nodes in all Python versions.\n   309→      No runtime annotation evaluation is required or appropriate here.\n   310→\n   311→   c. Record as injectable: (class_name, param_name, file_path, line)\n   312→3. For each injectable found:\n   313→   a. Search all Python files for call sites constructing that class\n   314→   b. Check if any call site provides the parameter by keyword\n   315→   c. If zero call sites provide it -> WiringFinding(unwired_callable)\n   316→```\n   317→\n   318→**Known Limitation — Import Aliases and Re-exports (tracked for v1.1)**\n   319→\n   320→The call-site search matches class names as they appear in the defining module.\n   321→Classes re-exported through `__init__.py` and consumed via aliases\n   322→(e.g., `from package import ClassName` where the package `__init__.py`\n   323→re-exports it) will not be resolved. This produces false positives for\n   324→re-exported classes.\n   325→\n   326→Expected FPR contribution in codebases using package-level re-exports:\n   327→30–70% of unwired-callable findings in shadow mode may be re-export false\n   328→positives. Phase 2 thresholds must be calibrated against Phase 1 data with\n   329→this in mind (see Section 8 threshold calibration guidance).\n   330→\n   331→Planned fix (v1.1): pre-pass alias map construction via `ast.Import` /\n   332→`ast.ImportFrom` traversal with `__init__.py` chain resolution (max 3 hops).\n   333→\n   334→**Pattern matched** (from forensic report):\n   335→```python\n   336→# This triggers detection:\n   337→class PortifyExecutor:\n   338→    def __init__(self, ..., step_runner: Optional[Callable] = None):\n   339→        ...\n   340→\n   341→# This call site does NOT provide step_runner:\n   342→executor = PortifyExecutor(steps=steps, workdir=workdir, ...)\n   343→# -> Finding: unwired_callable, PortifyExecutor.step_runner\n   344→```\n   345→\n   346→**Whitelist mechanism**: A `wiring_whitelist.yaml` file can list intentionally-optional\n   347→callables (event hooks, logging callbacks) excluded from analysis.\n   348→\n   349→**Schema**: each entry must conform to:\n   350→\n   351→```yaml\n   352→# wiring_whitelist.yaml\n   353→unwired_callables:\n   354→  - symbol: \"module.path.ClassName.param_name\"  # required; dotted path\n   355→    reason: \"string\"                             # required; non-empty\n   356→orphan_modules:\n   357→  - symbol: \"module.path.function_name\"          # required; dotted path\n   358→    reason: \"string\"                             # required; non-empty\n   359→unwired_registries:\n   360→  - symbol: \"registry.key.name\"                  # required; dotted path\n   361→    reason: \"string\"                             # required; non-empty\n   362→```\n   363→\n   364→The legacy `class` + `param` split form is accepted as equivalent to\n   365→`symbol: \"ClassName.param\"` and normalized on load.\n   366→\n   367→All three finding types (`unwired_callables`, `orphan_modules`, `unwired_registries`)\n   368→share the same entry schema (`symbol` + `reason`). The `whitelist_entries_applied`\n   369→frontmatter field (§4.3.2) counts matched entries across all three types.\n   370→\n   371→**Validation behavior (Phase 1 — shadow mode)**:\n   372→- `load_wiring_config()` MUST validate each entry against the schema above.\n   373→- Entries missing `symbol` or `reason`, or with an empty `reason`, are MALFORMED.\n   374→  Malformed entries MUST be skipped with a WARNING:\n   375→    `WARNING: wiring_whitelist.yaml entry [N] malformed (missing: <field>), skipping.`\n   376→- `load_wiring_config()` MUST NOT raise `WiringConfigError` for malformed entries\n   377→  during Phase 1 shadow mode — the gate must continue running to preserve\n   378→  observation data.\n   379→\n   380→**Phase 2 note**: `load_wiring_config()` will be updated to raise `WiringConfigError`\n   381→on any malformed entry before Phase 2 activation. Resolve all whitelist warnings\n   382→before Phase 2 cutover.\n   383→\n   384→#### 4.2.2 Orphan Module Analysis\n   385→\n   386→**Purpose**: Detect Python files in conventionally-structured directories (`steps/`,\n   387→`handlers/`, `validators/`) whose exported functions are never imported by any\n   388→consumer module.\n   389→\n   390→**Algorithm**:\n   391→\n   392→```\n   393→1. Identify \"provider directories\" by convention:\n   394→   - directories named steps/, handlers/, validators/, checks/\n   395→   Note: Heuristic detection (3+ files with common prefix) deferred to v1.1\n   396→   pending algorithm specification and test case definition.\n   397→2. For each Python file in a provider directory:\n   398→   a. AST-parse to extract top-level function definitions (excluding _private)\n   399→   b. For each exported function:\n   400→      - Search all Python files OUTSIDE the provider directory for:\n   401→        * import statements referencing the function\n   402→        * from ... import statements referencing the function\n   403→   c. If zero importers found -> WiringFinding(orphan_module)\n   404→```\n   405→\n   406→**Pattern matched** (from forensic report):\n   407→```python\n   408→# src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py\n   409→def run_validate_config():  # exported, but never imported by executor.py\n   410→    ...\n   411→\n   412→# executor.py never contains:\n   413→# from .steps.validate_config import run_validate_config\n   414→# -> Finding: orphan_module, steps/validate_config.py::run_validate_config\n   415→```\n   416→\n   417→**Exclusions**: `__init__.py`, files matching `conftest.py`, `test_*.py`.\n   418→\n   419→#### 4.2.3 Unwired Registry Analysis\n   420→\n   421→**Purpose**: Detect dictionary constants with naming patterns indicating dispatch\n   422→registries (`REGISTRY`, `DISPATCH`, `RUNNERS`, `HANDLERS`, `ROUTER`) whose values\n   423→reference functions that cannot be resolved via import.\n   424→\n   425→**Algorithm**:\n   426→\n   427→```\n   428→1. AST-parse all Python files\n   429→2. For each module-level assignment where:\n   430→   a. Target name matches REGISTRY_PATTERNS regex\n   431→   b. Value is a Dict literal\n   432→3. For each dict entry:\n   433→   a. Extract value (expected: function reference or string path)\n   434→   b. If value is a Name node: verify the name is importable in scope\n   435→   c. If value is a string: verify it resolves to a module.function path\n   436→4. Entries with unresolvable values -> WiringFinding(unwired_registry)\n   437→```\n   438→\n   439→**Registry patterns** (configurable):\n   440→```python\n   441→DEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS = re.compile(\n   442→    r\"^(STEP_REGISTRY|STEP_DISPATCH|PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS|\"\n   443→    r\"\\w*_REGISTRY|\\w*_DISPATCH|\\w*_HANDLERS|\\w*_ROUTER)$\"\n   444→)\n   445→```\n   446→\n   447→### 4.3 Report Format\n   448→\n   449→The wiring analysis emits a Markdown file with YAML frontmatter, conforming to\n   450→the `GateCriteria` validation pattern used by all existing gates.\n   451→\n   452→```markdown\n   453→---\n   454→gate: wiring-verification\n   455→target_dir: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify\n   456→files_analyzed: 14\n   457→unwired_count: 1\n   458→orphan_count: 2\n   459→registry_count: 0\n   460→total_findings: 3\n   461→analysis_complete: true\n   462→enforcement_scope: task\n   463→resolved_gate_mode: shadow\n   464→---\n   465→\n   466→# Wiring Verification Report\n   467→\n   468→## Unwired Callables (1)\n   469→\n   470→### WF-001: PortifyExecutor.step_runner\n   471→\n   472→- **File**: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/executor.py\n   473→- **Line**: 393\n   474→- **Type**: unwired_callable\n   475→- **Severity**: critical\n   476→- **Detail**: Constructor parameter `step_runner: Optional[Callable] = None` is never\n   477→  provided at any of 1 call sites. Call sites: `executor.py:1395 (run_portify)`.\n   478→\n   479→## Orphan Modules (2)\n   480→\n   481→### WF-002: steps/validate_config.py::run_validate_config\n   482→\n   483→- **File**: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py\n   484→- **Line**: 12\n   485→- **Type**: orphan_module\n   486→- **Severity**: critical\n   487→- **Detail**: Exported function `run_validate_config` has 0 importers across 14 files.\n   488→\n   489→### WF-003: steps/discover_components.py::run_discover_components\n   490→\n   491→- **File**: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/discover_components.py\n   492→- **Line**: 8\n   493→- **Type**: orphan_module\n   494→- **Severity**: critical\n   495→- **Detail**: Exported function `run_discover_components` has 0 importers across 14 files.\n   496→\n   497→## Summary\n   498→\n   499→3 findings (1 unwired callable, 2 orphan modules, 0 unwired registries).\n   500→Gate status: FAIL (enforcement: shadow -- logged only).\n   501→```\n   502→\n   503→**4.3.1 Frontmatter Serialization Requirements**\n   504→\n   505→The `emit_report` function (T05) MUST serialize all string-valued frontmatter\n   506→fields using `yaml.safe_dump()` rather than f-string or `str.format()` interpolation.\n   507→This applies to: `target_dir`, `symbol_name`, `detail`.\n   508→\n   509→Boolean and integer fields that are gate-evaluated (`analysis_complete`,\n   510→`unwired_count`, `orphan_count`, `registry_count`, `total_findings`) are\n   511→serialized as Python literals and are exempt from this requirement.\n   512→\n   513→**Rationale**: f-string interpolation of filesystem paths and symbol names into\n   514→YAML produces malformed output when values contain YAML-special characters (`:`,\n   515→`|`, `{`, `}`, `[`, `]`). While these cannot appear in Python identifiers, they\n   516→can appear in `target_dir` values. Malformed frontmatter causes report parse\n   517→errors; defensively handled, these produce gate failures rather than bypasses,\n   518→but the failure mode is confusing and avoidable.\n   519→\n   520→**Implementation pattern**:\n   521→```python\n   522→import yaml\n   523→metadata_fields = {\n   524→    \"target_dir\": str(target_dir),\n   525→    \"symbol_name\": finding.symbol_name,\n   526→    \"detail\": finding.detail,\n   527→}\n   528→frontmatter_str = yaml.safe_dump(metadata_fields, default_flow_style=False)\n   529→```\n   530→\n   531→**4.3.2 Whitelist Audit Visibility in Frontmatter**\n   532→\n   533→`emit_report()` MUST include the following field in YAML frontmatter:\n   534→\n   535→```yaml\n   536→whitelist_entries_applied: 0   # integer; count of entries that suppressed ≥1 finding\n   537→```\n   538→\n   539→This field is required regardless of whether a whitelist file is configured.\n   540→If no whitelist is configured or no entries matched, emit `whitelist_entries_applied: 0`.\n   541→\n   542→**Rationale**: reviewers must be able to detect whitelist-based suppression from\n   543→the gate report alone, without diffing `wiring_whitelist.yaml` across commits.\n   544→\n   545→### 4.4 Gate Definition\n   546→\n   547→```python\n   548→WIRING_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   549→    required_frontmatter_fields=[\n   550→        \"gate\",\n   551→        \"target_dir\",\n   552→        \"files_analyzed\",\n   553→        \"files_skipped\",\n   554→        \"unwired_count\",\n   555→        \"orphan_count\",\n   556→        \"registry_count\",\n   557→        \"total_findings\",\n   558→        \"analysis_complete\",\n   559→        \"enforcement_scope\",\n   560→        \"resolved_gate_mode\",\n   561→        \"whitelist_entries_applied\",\n   562→    ],\n   563→    min_lines=10,\n   564→    enforcement_tier=\"STRICT\",\n   565→    semantic_checks=[\n   566→        SemanticCheck(\n   567→            name=\"analysis_complete_true\",\n   568→            check_fn=_analysis_complete_true,\n   569→            failure_message=\"analysis_complete must be true\",\n   570→        ),\n   571→        SemanticCheck(\n   572→            name=\"zero_unwired_callables\",\n   573→            check_fn=_zero_unwired_callables,\n   574→            failure_message=\"unwired_count must be 0; all injectable callables must be provided\",\n   575→        ),\n   576→        SemanticCheck(\n   577→            name=\"zero_orphan_modules\",\n   578→            check_fn=_zero_orphan_modules,\n   579→            failure_message=\"orphan_count must be 0; all exported functions must have importers\",\n   580→        ),\n   581→        SemanticCheck(\n   582→            name=\"zero_unwired_registries\",\n   583→            check_fn=_zero_unwired_registries,\n   584→            failure_message=\"registry_count must be 0; all registry entries must resolve\",\n   585→        ),\n   586→        SemanticCheck(\n   587→            name=\"total_findings_consistent\",\n   588→            check_fn=_total_findings_consistent,\n   589→            failure_message=\"total_findings must equal unwired_count + orphan_count + registry_count\",\n   590→        ),\n   591→    ],\n   592→)\n   593→```\n   594→\n   595→The semantic check functions follow the established `(content: str) -> bool` pattern\n   596→used by `_high_severity_count_zero`, `_total_analyzed_consistent`, etc. in `roadmap/gates.py`.\n   597→\n   598→### 4.5 Sprint Integration\n   599→\n   600→The wiring gate hooks into the sprint runner at the post-task classification point.\n   601→\n   602→**Hook point**: `sprint/executor.py`, after `_classify_from_result_file()` returns,\n   603→before the task status is finalized.\n   604→\n   605→**TurnLedger-aware budget flow** (replaces `wiring_gate_mode` string-switch):\n   606→\n   607→```python\n   608→# In execute_phase_tasks() or _run_task_subprocess(), after classification:\n   609→# Hook signature: run_post_task_wiring_hook(task, config, ledger=None) -> WiringReport\n   610→\n   611→if not config.wiring_gate_enabled:\n   612→    # Skip wiring analysis entirely; no report emitted\n   613→    return\n   614→\n   615→# Budget debit (before analysis)\n   616→if ledger is not None:\n   617→    ledger.debit_wiring(WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS)\n   618→\n   619→# Run analysis\n   620→wiring_report_path = work_dir / f\"{task_id}-wiring-report.md\"\n   621→report = run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)\n   622→\n   623→# Resolve enforcement mode via scope-based resolution (replaces string switches)\n   624→mode = resolve_gate_mode(config.wiring_gate_scope, config.wiring_gate_grace_period)\n   625→\n   626→emit_report(report, wiring_report_path,\n   627→            enforcement_scope=config.wiring_gate_scope,\n   628→            resolved_gate_mode=mode)\n   629→\n   630→if report.passed:\n   631→    # Credit budget on pass (see Section 4.1.1 for floor-to-zero behavior)\n   632→    if ledger is not None:\n   633→        ledger.credit_wiring(WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS, config.reimbursement_rate)\n   634→    return report\n   635→\n   636→# Failure handling based on resolved mode\n   637→if mode == GateMode.BLOCKING:\n   638→    # NOTE (IE-5): This is the first production instantiation of SprintGatePolicy\n   639→    # in the wiring gate path. SprintGatePolicy's constructor requirements and\n   640→    # failure modes must be validated against trailing_gate.py's existing usage.\n   641→    policy = SprintGatePolicy(config)\n   642→\n   643→    if ledger is not None and ledger.can_run_wiring_gate(REMEDIATION_COST):\n   644→        # Remediation path (see Section 4.5.3 for full spec)\n   645→        failure_msg = _format_wiring_failure(report)\n   646→        remediation_step = policy.build_remediation_step(\n   647→            gate_name=\"wiring-verification\",\n   648→            failure_message=failure_msg,\n   649→            can_remediate=lambda: ledger.can_run_wiring_gate(REMEDIATION_COST),\n   650→            debit=lambda cost: ledger.debit_wiring(cost),\n   651→        )\n   652→        # Execute remediation, then recheck (Section 4.5.3)\n   653→    else:\n   654→        # No ledger or budget exhausted — direct FAIL (Section 4.5.2)\n   655→        logger.error(f\"Wiring gate FAIL: {report.total_findings} findings (no remediation)\")\n   656→\n   657→elif mode == GateMode.SHADOW:\n   658→    # Shadow mode: log and defer (no task status impact)\n   659→    logger.info(f\"[shadow] Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n   660→    # DeferredRemediationLog adapter (Gamma IE-4, Section 4.5.3)\n   661→    deferred_result = TrailingGateResult(\n   662→        step_id=f\"{task.task_id}_wiring\",\n   663→        gate_name=\"wiring-verification\",\n   664→        passed=False,\n   665→        findings=report.total_findings,\n   666→    )\n   667→    DeferredRemediationLog.append(deferred_result)\n   668→\n   669→elif mode == GateMode.SOFT:\n   670→    # Soft mode: warn in TUI but do not block\n   671→    if not report.passed:\n   672→        tui.warn(f\"Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n   673→\n   674→return report\n   675→```\n   676→\n   677→**Configuration**: Three fields on `SprintConfig` (replaces `wiring_gate_mode`, see Section 6.2):\n   678→\n   679→```python\n   680→wiring_gate_enabled: bool = True\n   681→wiring_gate_scope: GateScope = GateScope.TASK\n   682→wiring_gate_grace_period: int = 0\n   683→```\n   684→\n   685→#### 4.5.1 TurnLedger Budget Flow\n   686→\n   687→**Budget flow diagram** (complete debit-before-analysis, credit-on-pass path):\n   688→\n   689→```\n   690→+-------------------+\n   691→| Task completes    |\n   692→| (sprint runner)   |\n   693→+--------+----------+\n   694→         |\n   695→         v\n   696→+--------+----------+\n   697→| if ledger is not  |\n   698→| None:             |\n   699→|   ledger.debit_   |\n   700→|   wiring(WIRING_  |\n   701→|   ANALYSIS_TURNS) |\n   702→+--------+----------+\n   703→         |\n   704→         v\n   705→+--------+----------+\n   706→| run_wiring_       |\n   707→| analysis()        |\n   708→+--------+----------+\n   709→         |\n   710→         v\n   711→+--------+----------+\n   712→| mode = resolve_   |\n   713→| gate_mode(scope,  |\n   714→| grace_period)     |\n   715→+--------+----------+\n   716→         |\n   717→    +----+----+\n   718→    |         |\n   719→    v         v\n   720→  PASS      FAIL\n   721→    |         |\n   722→    v         +-------+-------+\n   723→+---+-------+ |               |\n   724→| if ledger | v               v\n   725→| is not    | BLOCKING        SHADOW/SOFT\n   726→| None:     | |               |\n   727→|  credit_  | v               v\n   728→|  wiring(  | attempt_        DeferredRemediation\n   729→|  turns,   | remediation()   Log.append()\n   730→|  rate)    | |               (synthetic\n   731→+---+-------+ v               TrailingGateResult)\n   732→    |         budget debit\n   733→    v         for retry\n   734→  DONE        |\n   735→              v\n   736→            _recheck_wiring()\n   737→```\n   738→\n   739→**Budget accounting table**:\n   740→\n   741→| Outcome | Debit | Credit | Net cost |\n   742→|---------|-------|--------|----------|\n   743→| Pass (single-turn, rate=0.8) | `WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS` (1) | `int(1 * 0.8)` = **0** | 1 turn |\n   744→| Pass (multi-turn, rate=0.8) | N turns | `int(N * 0.8)` | ~0.2N turns |\n   745→| Fail (BLOCKING, remediation succeeds) | N + remediation turns | credit on recheck pass | variable |\n   746→| Fail (BLOCKING, remediation fails) | N + remediation turns | 0 | N + remediation |\n   747→| Fail (shadow/soft) | N turns | 0 | N turns |\n   748→| Ledger is None | 0 (skipped) | 0 (skipped) | 0 (no tracking) |\n   749→\n   750→**Hook signature**:\n   751→\n   752→```python\n   753→def run_post_task_wiring_hook(\n   754→    task: Task,\n   755→    config: SprintConfig,\n   756→    ledger: TurnLedger | None = None,\n   757→) -> WiringReport:\n   758→    \"\"\"Post-task wiring analysis with optional budget tracking.\n   759→\n   760→    All budget operations gated by `if ledger is not None`.\n   761→    \"\"\"\n   762→```\n   763→\n   764→**BC-5 cross-release ordering note**: The wiring gate budget flow applies per-task within a\n   765→release. Cross-release ordering (e.g., v3.1 → v3.2 migration) preserves existing TurnLedger\n   766→state — `wiring_gate_cost` and `wiring_gate_credits` fields have zero defaults that accumulate\n   767→from first use. If v3.1 lands first and establishes `reimbursement_rate` activation, v3.2\n   768→becomes the second consumer. If v3.2 lands first, the `ledger is None` path provides\n   769→self-sufficient operation.\n   770→\n   771→#### 4.5.2 Backward Compatibility — TurnLedger is None\n   772→\n   773→**Null-ledger behavioral matrix**: When `ledger is None`, wiring analysis runs without budget\n   774→tracking. This preserves phase-level execution (pre-TurnLedger sprints).\n   775→\n   776→| Operation | `ledger is not None` | `ledger is None` |\n   777→|-----------|----------------------|-------------------|\n   778→| Budget debit | `ledger.debit_wiring(turns)` | Skip (no tracking) |\n   779→| Budget credit | `ledger.credit_wiring(turns, rate)` | Skip (no tracking) |\n   780→| Analysis | `run_wiring_analysis()` — runs normally | `run_wiring_analysis()` — runs normally |\n   781→| Mode resolution | `resolve_gate_mode(scope, grace_period)` | `resolve_gate_mode(scope, grace_period)` — same |\n   782→| Blocking failure | `attempt_remediation()` with budget tracking | Direct FAIL (no retry without budget tracking) |\n   783→| Shadow failure | `DeferredRemediationLog.append()` | `DeferredRemediationLog.append()` — same |\n   784→\n   785→**Key difference**: When `ledger is None` and a BLOCKING failure occurs, the gate issues a\n   786→direct FAIL with no remediation attempt. Remediation requires budget tracking to debit the\n   787→retry cost. Without a ledger, the system cannot account for remediation turns and must fail\n   788→immediately.\n   789→\n   790→#### 4.5.3 Remediation Path on Wiring Gate Failure\n   791→\n   792→**1. `attempt_remediation()` integration (BLOCKING mode)**:\n   793→\n   794→Uses a callable-based interface to avoid direct TurnLedger import in `trailing_gate.py`:\n   795→\n   796→```python\n   797→# Callable-based interface for remediation\n   798→can_remediate: Callable[[], bool]  # checks budget availability\n   799→debit: Callable[[int], None]       # debits remediation cost\n   800→\n   801→# In executor hook:\n   802→if can_remediate():\n   803→    debit(REMEDIATION_COST)\n   804→    # ... run remediation subprocess\n   805→```\n   806→\n   807→**2. `_format_wiring_failure()` helper spec**:\n   808→\n   809→```python\n   810→def _format_wiring_failure(report: WiringReport) -> str:\n   811→    \"\"\"Format wiring findings into human-readable failure message for remediation step.\n   812→\n   813→    Returns a structured string listing each finding with file, line, and detail.\n   814→    Used as input to the remediation subprocess.\n   815→    \"\"\"\n   816→```\n   817→\n   818→**3. `_recheck_wiring()` helper spec**:\n   819→\n   820→```python\n   821→def _recheck_wiring(target_dir: Path, config: WiringConfig) -> WiringReport:\n   822→    \"\"\"Re-run wiring analysis after remediation attempt.\n   823→\n   824→    Returns a fresh WiringReport. If the recheck passes, the remediation\n   825→    is considered successful and credits are issued.\n   826→    \"\"\"\n   827→```\n   828→\n   829→**4. `DeferredRemediationLog` adapter** (Gamma IE-4):\n   830→\n   831→Shadow mode deferred logging requires constructing a synthetic `TrailingGateResult` from\n   832→wiring findings, since `DeferredRemediationLog.append()` takes `TrailingGateResult`, not\n   833→`WiringReport`:\n   834→\n   835→```python\n   836→# Adapter: WiringReport -> TrailingGateResult\n   837→deferred_result = TrailingGateResult(\n   838→    step_id=f\"{task.task_id}_wiring\",\n   839→    gate_name=\"wiring-verification\",\n   840→    passed=False,\n   841→    findings=report.total_findings,\n   842→)\n   843→DeferredRemediationLog.append(deferred_result)\n   844→```\n   845→\n   846→**5. Budget flow during remediation**:\n   847→\n   848→- Additional debit of `REMEDIATION_COST` turns before remediation attempt\n   849→- Credit issued only if `_recheck_wiring()` passes\n   850→- Net cost on successful remediation: `WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS + REMEDIATION_COST - credit`\n   851→- Net cost on failed remediation: `WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS + REMEDIATION_COST` (no credit)\n   852→\n   853→**6. Edge cases**:\n   854→\n   855→- **Budget exhaustion mid-remediation**: `can_remediate()` returns False → skip remediation,\n   856→  issue direct FAIL. Log `WARN: budget-exhausted-skipping-remediation`.\n   857→- **Subprocess failure**: Remediation subprocess exits non-zero → treat as failed remediation,\n   858→  no credit, log error with subprocess exit code.\n   859→- **Gate re-evaluation**: After remediation, full `_recheck_wiring()` runs. If new findings\n   860→  appear (remediation introduced new issues), the recheck FAIL is final — no recursive\n   861→  remediation attempts.\n   862→\n   863→#### 4.5.4 KPI Report Extensions\n   864→\n   865→**New `GateKPIReport` fields** (6 wiring-specific fields):\n   866→\n   867→```python\n   868→# On GateKPIReport (sprint/kpi.py)\n   869→wiring_total_debits: int       # Sum of all wiring gate debits\n   870→wiring_total_credits: int      # Sum of all wiring gate credits\n   871→wiring_net_cost: int           # wiring_total_debits - wiring_total_credits\n   872→wiring_analyses_run: int       # Count of wiring analyses executed\n   873→wiring_findings_total: int     # Sum of total_findings across all analyses\n   874→wiring_remediations_attempted: int  # Count of remediation attempts\n   875→```\n   876→\n   877→**`build_kpi_report()` signature update**:\n   878→\n   879→```python\n   880→def build_kpi_report(\n   881→    ...,\n   882→    wiring_ledger: TurnLedger | None = None,\n   883→) -> GateKPIReport:\n   884→    \"\"\"Build KPI report with optional wiring metrics from TurnLedger.\"\"\"\n   885→```\n   886→\n   887→**New file entry**: `sprint/kpi.py` MODIFY +15-20 LOC.\n   888→\n   889→**Note**: Generalization to generic `gate_family_counts: dict[str, int]` is deferred to v3.3\n   890→(per brainstorm.md Proposal B).\n   891→\n   892→### 4.6 Companion: Deviation Count Reconciliation\n   893→\n   894→This release also includes the Deviation Count Reconciliation Gate (Proposal 4 from\n   895→the ranking), as a zero-cost companion that strengthens existing Link 1 gates.\n   896→\n   897→**Implementation**: Single function `_deviation_counts_reconciled(content: str) -> bool`\n   898→added to `SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE.semantic_checks` in `roadmap/gates.py`.\n   899→\n   900→**Algorithm**:\n   901→1. Parse frontmatter for `high_severity_count`, `medium_severity_count`, `low_severity_count`\n   902→2. Regex-scan body for `DEV-\\d{3}` entries, extract severity from `**Severity**: X` lines\n   903→3. Compare body counts to frontmatter counts\n   904→4. Fail on any mismatch\n   905→\n   906→**Estimated LOC**: 35-50 lines.\n   907→\n   908→---\n   909→\n   910→## 5. File Manifest\n   911→\n   912→| File | Action | Estimated LOC | Purpose |\n   913→|------|--------|---------------|---------|\n   914→| `src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py` | CREATE | 250-300 | Core analysis engine, report emitter, gate definition |\n   915→| `src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_config.py` | CREATE | 40-60 | Configuration dataclass, patterns, whitelist loader |\n   916→| `src/superclaude/cli/sprint/models.py` | MODIFY | +30-35 | TurnLedger extensions (3 fields, 3 methods) + SprintConfig scope-based fields |\n   917→| `src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py` | MODIFY | +50-70 | TurnLedger-aware wiring hook, resolve_gate_mode(), remediation path |\n   918→| `src/superclaude/cli/sprint/kpi.py` | MODIFY | +15-20 | GateKPIReport wiring extensions |\n   919→| `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/gates.py` | MODIFY | +40 | `_deviation_counts_reconciled` semantic check |\n   920→| `tests/audit/test_wiring_gate.py` | CREATE | 200-250 | Unit tests for all analysis functions |\n   921→| `tests/audit/test_deviation_recon.py` | CREATE | 60-80 | Unit tests for deviation count reconciliation |\n   922→| `tests/audit/fixtures/` | CREATE | 50-80 | Python fixtures for wiring analysis tests |\n   923→| `tests/pipeline/test_full_flow.py` | MODIFY | +80-100 | Budget integration test scenarios 5-8 |\n   924→\n   925→**Total new production code**: ~410-500 lines\n   926→**Total new test code**: ~400-520 lines\n   927→\n   928→---\n   929→\n   930→## 6. Interface Contracts\n   931→\n   932→### 6.1 Public API\n   933→\n   934→```python\n   935→# Entry point for wiring analysis\n   936→def run_wiring_analysis(\n   937→    target_dir: Path,\n   938→    config: WiringConfig | None = None,\n   939→) -> WiringReport:\n   940→    \"\"\"Analyze a directory for wiring verification issues.\n   941→\n   942→    Args:\n   943→        target_dir: Root directory to analyze (e.g., src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/).\n   944→        config: Optional configuration overriding defaults.\n   945→\n   946→    Returns:\n   947→        WiringReport with all findings.\n   948→    \"\"\"\n   949→\n   950→# Report emitter (Markdown + YAML frontmatter)\n   951→def emit_report(\n   952→    report: WiringReport,\n   953→    output_path: Path,\n   954→    enforcement_scope: GateScope = GateScope.TASK,\n   955→    resolved_gate_mode: GateMode = GateMode.SHADOW,\n   956→) -> None:\n   957→    \"\"\"Write wiring report as Markdown with YAML frontmatter.\n   958→\n   959→    The output conforms to the GateCriteria validation pattern:\n   960→    frontmatter fields match WIRING_GATE.required_frontmatter_fields.\n   961→    \"\"\"\n   962→\n   963→# SemanticCheck-compatible function\n   964→def check_wiring_report(content: str) -> bool:\n   965→    \"\"\"Validate a wiring report passes all criteria.\n   966→\n   967→    Used as check_fn in SemanticCheck instances on WIRING_GATE.\n   968→    \"\"\"\n   969→```\n   970→\n   971→### 6.2 Configuration Contract\n   972→\n   973→```python\n   974→@dataclass\n   975→class WiringConfig:\n   976→    \"\"\"Configuration for wiring verification analysis.\"\"\"\n   977→\n   978→    # Patterns identifying dispatch registries\n   979→    registry_patterns: re.Pattern = DEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS\n   980→\n   981→    # Directories treated as \"provider\" directories for orphan analysis.\n   982→    # IMPORTANT: must be set to match the target repository's actual provider\n   983→    # directory conventions before shadow mode activation.\n   984→    # The default value {\"steps\", \"handlers\", \"validators\", \"checks\"} reflects\n   985→    # common framework conventions and will produce zero orphan findings (a false\n   986→    # clean result) in codebases using different naming (e.g., \"audit/\",\n   987→    # \"execution/\", \"pm_agent/\"). This field is not optional for production deployments.\n   988→    # See Section 8 pre-activation checklist.\n   989→    provider_dir_names: frozenset[str] = frozenset({\n   990→        \"steps\", \"handlers\", \"validators\", \"checks\",\n   991→    })\n   992→\n   993→    # Path to wiring_whitelist.yaml. Entries suppress gate findings for matched symbols.\n   994→    # See Section 4.2.1 for entry schema and validation behavior.\n   995→    # Count of applied entries is reported in gate output frontmatter (Section 4.3.2).\n   996→    whitelist_path: Path | None = None\n   997→\n   998→    # File exclusion patterns\n   999→    exclude_patterns: list[str] = field(default_factory=lambda: [\n  1000→        \"test_*.py\", \"conftest.py\", \"__init__.py\",\n  1001→    ])\n  1002→```\n  1003→\n  1004→**SprintConfig wiring gate fields** (replaces `wiring_gate_mode`):\n  1005→\n  1006→```python\n  1007→# On SprintConfig (sprint/models.py)\n  1008→SHADOW_GRACE_INFINITE: int = 999_999  # Named constant for shadow phase grace period\n  1009→\n  1010→wiring_gate_enabled: bool = True\n  1011→wiring_gate_scope: GateScope = GateScope.TASK\n  1012→wiring_gate_grace_period: int = 0\n  1013→```\n  1014→\n  1015→**Old-to-new mapping** (`wiring_gate_mode` → scope-based fields):\n  1016→\n  1017→| Old `wiring_gate_mode` | `wiring_gate_enabled` | `wiring_gate_scope` | `wiring_gate_grace_period` |\n  1018→|-------------------------|-----------------------|----------------------|----------------------------|\n  1019→| `\"off\"` | `False` | (ignored) | (ignored) |\n  1020→| `\"shadow\"` | `True` | `GateScope.TASK` | `SHADOW_GRACE_INFINITE` |\n  1021→| `\"soft\"` | `True` | `GateScope.TASK` | `0` |\n  1022→| `\"full\"` | `True` | `GateScope.TASK` | `0` |\n  1023→\n  1024→**Migration note** (`__post_init__`): Defensive only — `wiring_gate_mode` is v3.2-new code,\n  1025→not yet shipped. Only `run_post_task_wiring_hook()` and `run_wiring_safeguard_checks()` read\n  1026→this field. Emit deprecation warning if `wiring_gate_mode` is set. Remove after 1 release.\n  1027→\n  1028→### 6.3 Gate Contract\n  1029→\n  1030→The `WIRING_GATE` constant conforms to `GateCriteria` and is evaluated by the\n  1031→existing `gate_passed()` function in `pipeline/gates.py` without modification.\n  1032→\n  1033→**Frontmatter contract** (must appear in every report):\n  1034→\n  1035→| Field | Type | Constraint |\n  1036→|-------|------|-----------|\n  1037→| `gate` | string | Must be `\"wiring-verification\"` |\n  1038→| `target_dir` | string | Non-empty |\n  1039→| `files_analyzed` | int | >= 0 |\n  1040→| `files_skipped` | int | >= 0; count of Python files that failed AST parsing |\n  1041→| `unwired_count` | int | Must be 0 for gate pass |\n  1042→| `orphan_count` | int | Must be 0 for gate pass |\n  1043→| `registry_count` | int | Must be 0 for gate pass |\n  1044→| `total_findings` | int | Must equal sum of above three |\n  1045→| `analysis_complete` | bool | Must be true |\n  1046→| `enforcement_scope` | string | GateScope value; derived from `resolve_gate_mode()` at report generation |\n  1047→| `resolved_gate_mode` | string | GateMode value; derived from `resolve_gate_mode()` output |\n  1048→| `whitelist_entries_applied` | int | >= 0; count of whitelist entries that suppressed findings |\n  1049→\n  1050→---\n  1051→\n  1052→## 7. Risk Assessment\n  1053→\n  1054→| Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation |\n  1055→|------|-----------|--------|-----------|\n  1056→| R1: False positives from intentional `Optional[Callable]` hooks | High | Medium | Whitelist mechanism (`wiring_whitelist.yaml`) |\n  1057→| R2: AST parsing fails on complex Python patterns | Medium | Low | Graceful degradation: log warning, skip file, do not fail gate |\n  1058→| R3: Shadow mode collects insufficient data | Low | Medium | Shadow mode runs for minimum 2 releases before enforcement decision |\n  1059→| R4: Performance impact on sprint loop | Low | Medium | Wiring analysis is AST-only, no subprocess; expected < 2s for 50-file packages |\n  1060→| R5: Naming convention heuristics miss new registry patterns | Medium | Low | Configurable `registry_patterns` regex; log when no registries found |\n  1061→| R6: `provider_dir_names` mismatch with actual codebase conventions | High | High | Pre-activation validation checklist (Section 8 Phase 1); zero-findings sanity check required on first run |\n  1062→| R7: `int(turns * reimbursement_rate)` floors to zero at `WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS=1` | High | Medium | Tests explicitly assert `wiring_gate_credits == 0` (see Section 4.1.1 floor behavior documentation); `reimbursement_rate` effectively inert for single-turn debits unless set to 1.0 |\n  1063→| R8: SprintConfig field rename (`wiring_gate_mode` → 3 fields) breaks development branch configs | Medium | Low | `__post_init__` migration shim with deprecation warning; v3.2-new code only (no production consumers per Section 6.2) |\n  1064→\n  1065→---\n  1066→\n  1067→## 8. Rollout Plan\n  1068→\n  1069→### Phase 1: Shadow (this release)\n  1070→\n  1071→**SprintConfig profile**:\n  1072→```python\n  1073→wiring_gate_enabled = True\n  1074→wiring_gate_scope = GateScope.TASK\n  1075→wiring_gate_grace_period = SHADOW_GRACE_INFINITE  # 999_999 (Section 6.2)\n  1076→```\n  1077→\n  1078→**Pre-activation checklist (blocking — shadow mode must not start until both pass):**\n  1079→\n  1080→1. **Provider directory validation**: Confirm that at least one directory matching\n  1081→   `provider_dir_names` exists in the target repository and contains at least one\n  1082→   Python file. If zero matches are found, update `provider_dir_names` in\n  1083→   `WiringConfig` before proceeding. A shadow run against a misconfigured\n  1084→   `provider_dir_names` produces a silent null result indistinguishable from a\n  1085→   genuinely clean codebase and corrupts baseline data.\n  1086→\n  1087→2. **Zero-findings sanity check**: If the first shadow run produces zero findings\n  1088→   across ALL analyzers on a repository with >50 Python files, treat this as a\n  1089→   configuration error requiring investigation, not a passing result.\n  1090→   Log `WARN: zero-findings-on-first-run` and halt baseline collection until\n  1091→   the configuration is verified.\n  1092→\n  1093→- Wiring analysis runs after every task in sprint execution\n  1094→- Results logged to `.sprint-state/wiring/` directory\n  1095→- No impact on task status or pipeline flow\n  1096→- Collect baseline: false positive rate, finding distribution, analysis time\n  1097→\n  1098→### Phase 2: Soft (release +1, pending shadow data review)\n  1099→\n  1100→**SprintConfig profile** (transition from Phase 1: change `wiring_gate_grace_period`):\n  1101→```python\n  1102→wiring_gate_enabled = True\n  1103→wiring_gate_scope = GateScope.TASK\n  1104→wiring_gate_grace_period = 0\n  1105→```\n  1106→\n  1107→- Findings surfaced as warnings in sprint TUI\n  1108→- Findings recorded in `DeferredRemediationLog`\n  1109→- Block only at release scope (per `resolve_gate_mode()` which returns BLOCKING for release)\n  1110→- Override available via `--skip-wiring-gate` flag\n  1111→\n  1112→**Threshold calibration for known FPR sources**:\n  1113→\n  1114→When setting Phase 2 activation thresholds from Phase 1 baseline data,\n  1115→explicitly account for the following known false-positive sources:\n  1116→\n  1117→| Source | Expected FPR contribution | v1.0 mitigation | Planned fix |\n  1118→|---|---|---|---|\n  1119→| Re-exported classes (import aliases) | 30–70% of unwired-callable findings | Raise Phase 2 unwired-callable threshold; document noise floor | v1.1 alias pre-pass |\n  1120→| `provider_dir_names` misconfiguration | 100% of orphan-module findings (silent) | Pre-activation validation checklist (Section 8 Phase 1) | N/A — config |\n  1121→\n  1122→**Decision rule**: Phase 2 MUST NOT be activated if Phase 1 unwired-callable\n  1123→FPR cannot be separated from the re-export noise floor. Document the estimated\n  1124→noise floor in the Phase 1 report. Set Phase 2 thresholds at\n  1125→`measured_FPR + 2σ` above the noise floor estimate, not above zero.\n  1126→\n  1127→### Phase 3: Full (release +2, pending soft data review)\n  1128→\n  1129→**SprintConfig profile** (transition from Phase 2: change `wiring_gate_scope`):\n  1130→```python\n  1131→wiring_gate_enabled = True\n  1132→wiring_gate_scope = GateScope.RELEASE\n  1133→wiring_gate_grace_period = 0\n  1134→```\n  1135→\n  1136→- Findings block task completion at STRICT tier\n  1137→- Remediation via `SprintGatePolicy.build_remediation_step()`\n  1138→- No override without explicit whitelist entry\n  1139→\n  1140→### Rollout Decision Criteria\n  1141→\n  1142→| Metric | Shadow → Soft Threshold | Soft → Full Threshold | Debit on analysis | Credit on pass |\n  1143→|--------|--------------------------|------------------------|-------------------|----------------|\n  1144→| False positive rate | < 15% of findings are whitelisted | < 5% | Yes (WIRING_ANALYSIS_TURNS) | Yes (if pass) |\n  1145→| True positive rate | > 50% of findings are genuine bugs | > 80% | Yes | No (fail path) |\n  1146→| Analysis time p95 | < 5 seconds | < 3 seconds | Yes | Conditional |\n  1147→| Whitelist stability | Whitelist unchanged for 2+ sprints | Whitelist unchanged for 5+ sprints | Yes | Conditional |\n  1148→\n  1149→### Rollout Transition Checklist\n  1150→\n  1151→- [ ] Verify Phase N baseline data meets threshold criteria\n  1152→- [ ] Update `wiring_gate_scope` and/or `wiring_gate_grace_period` in SprintConfig\n  1153→- [ ] Confirm all whitelisted entries have valid `reason` fields\n  1154→- [ ] Run single-sprint dry run with new config profile\n  1155→- [ ] Review budget impact (debit/credit totals from GateKPIReport)\n  1156→- [ ] Announce transition to team; document in release notes\n  1157→\n  1158→**BC-5 cross-release ordering**: Phase transitions across releases preserve TurnLedger state.\n  1159→When upgrading from v3.1 → v3.2, existing `wiring_gate_cost` and `wiring_gate_credits` fields\n  1160→have zero defaults and accumulate from first use. Config field compatibility is maintained\n  1161→via `__post_init__` migration (Section 6.2).\n  1162→\n  1163→### Rollout Framework Integration\n  1164→\n  1165→This rollout plan SHOULD adopt the Unified Audit Gating rollout infrastructure (SS7.1/SS7.2 profiles, override governance, rollback triggers) rather than defining independent thresholds. The thresholds in this section serve as initial values to be configured within that framework.\n  1166→\n  1167→### Implementation Coordination\n  1168→\n  1169→When modifying `roadmap/gates.py`, coordinate with:\n  1170→- Anti-Instincts (`ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE` addition)\n  1171→- Unified Audit Gating (D-03/D-04 `SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE` extensions)\n  1172→\n  1173→Preferred approach: single coordinated PR or sequenced PRs with explicit rebase points to avoid merge conflicts.\n  1174→\n  1175→---\n  1176→\n  1177→## 9. Testing Strategy\n  1178→\n  1179→### 9.1 Coverage Requirements\n  1180→\n  1181→The test suite shall validate the wiring analysis gate across two layers.\n  1182→\n  1183→#### Unit Tests (minimum 14 tests, across 4 analyzer functions)\n  1184→\n  1185→**analyze_unwired_callables** (minimum 4 tests):\n  1186→- Positive: detects a callable parameter with `Optional[Callable] = None` that\n  1187→  has zero call sites providing it — produces 1 `WiringFinding(unwired_callable)`\n  1188→- Negative: same class, call site provides the parameter by keyword —\n  1189→  produces 0 findings\n  1190→- Whitelist: parameter matches a whitelist entry — produces 0 findings\n  1191→- Parse error: source file with a Python syntax error — gate does not crash;\n  1192→  logs a warning; `analysis_complete` field reflects degraded state\n  1193→- **Out of scope** (dynamic dispatch exclusion, Section 2): alias-based\n  1194→  injection and `**kwargs`-forwarded injection do not require test cases\n  1195→\n  1196→**analyze_orphan_modules** (minimum 5 tests):\n  1197→- Positive: function in a provider directory with zero importers —\n  1198→  produces 1 `WiringFinding(orphan_module)`\n  1199→- Negative (direct import): same function, explicitly imported by consumer —\n  1200→  produces 0 findings\n  1201→- Negative (`__init__.py` re-export): function re-exported via package\n  1202→  `__init__.py` and consumed transitively — produces 0 findings\n  1203→- Private function (`_name` prefix): excluded from analysis — produces 0 findings\n  1204→- `conftest.py`: pytest infrastructure files excluded — produces 0 findings\n  1205→\n  1206→**analyze_unwired_registries** (minimum 2 tests):\n  1207→- Positive: registry entry whose value symbol cannot be resolved —\n  1208→  produces 1 `WiringFinding(unwired_registry)`\n  1209→- Negative: registry entry whose value symbol resolves correctly —\n  1210→  produces 0 findings\n  1211→\n  1212→**TurnLedger model tests** (in `test_models.py`):\n  1213→- `test_debit_wiring`: verify `wiring_gate_cost` increments correctly\n  1214→- `test_credit_wiring`: verify `wiring_gate_credits` uses `int(turns * rate)` floor behavior\n  1215→- `test_can_run_wiring_gate`: verify budget check returns correct boolean\n  1216→\n  1217→**emit_report / gate** (minimum 3 tests):\n  1218→- Findings present → `gate_passed()` returns `(False, reason)`; report\n  1219→  frontmatter has non-zero count fields\n  1220→- No findings → `gate_passed()` returns `(True, None)`; report frontmatter\n  1221→  has all count fields == 0\n  1222→- YAML-safe serialization: a report emitted when `target_dir` contains a\n  1223→  YAML-special character (e.g., colon) and `symbol_name` contains a block\n  1224→  indicator character must parse without `yaml.YAMLError`; `gate_passed()`\n  1225→  must return the expected result based on finding counts\n  1226→\n  1227→### 9.2 Integration Tests (minimum 2 tests)\n  1228→\n  1229→**SC-010: cli-portify fixture integration**\n  1230→\n  1231→A dedicated fixture module set shall exist under `tests/audit/fixtures/`.\n  1232→The fixture must contain:\n  1233→- A source file defining a class with a constructor parameter typed\n  1234→  `Optional[Callable]` with a `None` default\n  1235→- A second source file that instantiates that class without providing the\n  1236→  callable parameter\n  1237→\n  1238→Behavioral contract (non-negotiable): `run_wiring_analysis()` on the fixture\n  1239→directory MUST produce exactly 1 `WiringFinding` of type `\"unwired_callable\"`\n  1240→identifying the specific class and parameter. Zero findings or more than 1\n  1241→finding constitutes test failure.\n  1242→\n  1243→The fixture file structure, class names, parameter names, and module layout\n  1244→are implementation decisions finalized at T06. Only the behavioral contract\n  1245→above is fixed by this specification.\n  1246→\n  1247→**SC-006: sprint shadow mode non-interference**\n  1248→\n  1249→When the wiring gate executes in shadow mode within a sprint run, the following\n  1250→must hold after gate execution regardless of gate outcome:\n  1251→- Task status fields (state, assignee, priority) in the sprint manifest are\n  1252→  unchanged\n  1253→- No exception is propagated to the sprint runner\n  1254→- A `logger.info(...)` or equivalent trace is emitted with finding count\n  1255→\n  1256→### 9.3 Test Infrastructure\n  1257→\n  1258→**Fixture directory**: `tests/audit/fixtures/` (existing in file manifest)\n  1259→**Size budget**: 50–80 LOC total (unchanged)\n  1260→**Coverage target**: ≥ 90% line coverage on `src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py`\n  1261→\n  1262→All WiringFinding `finding_type` values (`\"unwired_callable\"`, `\"orphan_module\"`,\n  1263→`\"unwired_registry\"`) must appear in at least one test assertion.\n  1264→Gate exit paths (pass and fail) must each appear in at least one test assertion.\n  1265→\n  1266→### 9.4 Budget Integration Tests\n  1267→\n  1268→Budget integration tests in `tests/pipeline/test_full_flow.py` (+80-100 LOC).\n  1269→Existing scenarios 1-4 are unchanged. New scenarios are additive.\n  1270→\n  1271→**Scenario 5 — Wiring pass budget credit**:\n  1272→Sprint task completes, wiring analysis passes. Verify `ledger.wiring_gate_credits` reflects\n  1273→credit. **Critical**: assert `wiring_gate_credits == 0` (not `== 1`) due to\n  1274→`int(1 * 0.8) = 0` floor behavior (Section 4.1.1). Only multi-turn analyses at rate < 1.0\n  1275→produce non-zero credits.\n  1276→\n  1277→**Scenario 6 — Wiring fail remediation (BLOCKING)**:\n  1278→Wiring analysis fails in BLOCKING mode. `attempt_remediation()` called. Verify:\n  1279→- Remediation step created via `SprintGatePolicy.build_remediation_step()`\n  1280→- Budget debited for both analysis and remediation attempt\n  1281→- `_recheck_wiring()` called after remediation\n  1282→\n  1283→**Scenario 7 — Ledger=None backward compatibility**:\n  1284→Wiring analysis runs without budget tracking when `ledger is None`.
